problems result in a four-point deduction.

    (a) For complex numbers z1 , z2 ∈ C, z1 + z2 = z1 + z2

CS 4134 – Quantum Computation and Information Processing
                                              Assignment 2
                        Virginia Tech Department of Computer Science, Spring 2026
                                        Instructor: Sumeet Khatri

Issue date: Thursday, February 5, 2026
Due date: Tuesday, February 10, 2026
Instructions: Please show all of your work. Your grade will be based not only on getting the correct answer,
but having a complete solution. You may work in collaboration with others, but you must write your own
solutions, in your own words. Use of AI tools is not prohibited, but be prepared to explain your solutions
and demonstrate your understanding to me on the board upon request at any time. Sticking to the deadline
is to your benefit, but there is no late penalty. If you would like the assignment to count towards your final
grade, then submit it before the final day of class in May. Submit a physical copy in class or an electronic
copy via Canvas.
Grading: You will start from a grade of 100%. For every missed step, unclear or unexplained step, and
mistake, you will lose two points, with a maximum of 10 points of deduction per problem. Unattempted
problems result in a four-point deduction.


1. (a) State the definition of a d × d Hermitian matrix in dimension d ∈ {2, 3, . . . }.
   (b) Write down the most general form of a 2 × 2 Hermitian matrix.
   (c) Prove that every d × d Hermitian matrix has real eigenvalues.


2. Draw a Bloch sphere and label the following locations.
   (a) Where a qubit is |0⟩ and |1⟩.
   (b) Where a qubit is |+⟩ and |−⟩.
   (c) Where a qubit is |+ i⟩ and |− i⟩.


3. (a) State the three-part mathematical definition of a density operator, and explain each part of the
       definition.
   (b) State the mathematical definition of the purity of a quantum state.
   (c) Write down an example of a pure quantum state for one qubit.

CS 4134 — Quantum Computation and Information Processing

Assignment 2

Virginia Tech Department of Computer Science, Spring 2026
Instructor: Sumeet Khatri

Issue date: Thursday, February 5, 2026
Due date: Tuesday, February 10, 2026

Instructions: Please show all of your work. Your grade will be based not only on getting the correct answer,
but having a complete solution. You may work in collaboration with others, but you must write your own
solutions, in your own words. Use of AI tools is not prohibited, but be prepared to explain your solutions
and demonstrate your understanding to me on the board upon request at any time. Sticking to the deadline
is to your benefit, but there is no late penalty. If you would like the assignment to count towards your final
grade, then submit it before the final day of class in May. Submit a physical copy in class or an electronic
copy via Canvas.

Grading: You will start from a grade of 100%. For every missed step, unclear or unexplained step, and
mistake, you will lose two points, with a maximum of 10 points of deduction per problem. Unattempted
problems result in a four-point deduction.

1. (a) State the definition of a d x d Hermitian matrix in dimension d € {2,3,...}.
(b) Write down the most general form of a 2 x 2 Hermitian matrix.

(c) Prove that every d x d Hermitian matrix has real eigenvalues.

2. Draw a Bloch sphere and label the following locations.
(a) Where a qubit is |0) and |1).
(b) Where a qubit is |+) and |—).
(c) Where a qubit is |+ i) and |— i).

3. (a) State the three-part mathematical definition of a density operator, and explain each part of the
definition.
(b) State the mathematical definition of the purity of a quantum state.

(c) Write down an example of a pure quantum state for one qubit.

CS 4134 – Quantum Computation and Information Processing
                                                 Assignment 4
                         Virginia Tech Department of Computer Science, Spring 2026
                                         Instructor: Sumeet Khatri

Issue date: Tuesday, February 24, 2026
Due date: Tuesday, March 3, 2026
Instructions: Please show all of your work. Your grade will be based not only on getting the correct answer,
but having a complete solution. You may work in collaboration with others, but you must write your own
solutions, in your own words. Use of AI tools is not prohibited, but be prepared to explain your solutions
and demonstrate your understanding to me on the board upon request at any time. Sticking to the deadline
is to your benefit, but there is no late penalty. If you would like the assignment to count towards your final
grade, then submit it before the final day of class in May. Submit a physical copy in class or an electronic
copy via Canvas.
Grading: You will start from a grade of 100%. For every missed step, unclear or unexplained step, and
mistake, you will lose two points, with a maximum of 10 points of deduction per problem. Unattempted
problems result in a 10-point deduction. You must submit the assignment with at least one problem attempted
in order to get a grade. Blank submissions will receive a grade of zero.


1. Consider the bipartite state ρAB = 12 |0, 0⟩⟨0, 0|AB + |1, 1⟩⟨1, 1|AB of Alice (A) and Bob (B).
                                                                        

    (a) If Alice and Bob both measure in the {|0⟩, |1⟩} basis, then prove that their outcomes are correlated,
        i.e., Pr[0, 0] = Pr[1, 1] = 12 and Pr[0, 1] = Pr[1, 0] = 0. Calculate the post-measurement states of
        Bob’s qubit conditioned on Alice’s two outcomes, and demonstrate that Bob always gets the same
        outcome as Alice.
    (b) Now suppose that Alice and Bob both measure in the {|+⟩, |−⟩} basis. Prove that their measurement
        outcomes are now completely uncorrelated: regardless of what outcome Alice gets, Bob’s outcomes
        are completely random.


2. Consider two arbitrary state vectors, |ψ1 ⟩ = α1 |0⟩+β1 |1⟩ and |ψ2 ⟩ = α2 |0⟩+β2 |1⟩, where α1 , β1 , α2 , β2 ∈ C.
   Prove that there does not exist any choices of α1 , β1 , α2 , β2 such that |ψ1 ⟩⊗|ψ2 ⟩ = |Φ+ ⟩ = √12 (|0, 0⟩+|1, 1⟩).
   Hence |Φ+ ⟩ is an entangled state vector.


3. For a density operator ρ ∈ L(Cd ), consider a spectral/eigenvalue decomposition as follows: ρ =
   Pd
     k=1 λk |ψk ⟩⟨ψk |, where λk are the eigenvalues and |ψk ⟩ are the associated eigenvectors.
    (a) What properties do the eigenvectors and eigenvalues have based on the definition of eignenval-
        ues/eigenvectors and the three-part definition of a density operator?
                                                   √
    (b) Write down the square root of ρ, denoted ρ or ρ1/2 , in terms of the spectral decomposition given
        above.
                                √          √
    (c) Prove that |ψρ ⟩ := vec( ρ) = (1 ⊗ ρ)|Γ⟩ is a purification of ρ.
                           Pd √
    (d) Show that |ψρ ⟩ = k=1 λk |ψk ⟩ ⊗ |ψk ⟩.


4. Let X, Y, Z denote the Pauli operators. Prove the following identities.
    (a) 14 12 ⊗ 12 + X ⊗ X − Y ⊗ Y + Z ⊗ Z = |Φ+ ⟩⟨Φ+ |.

5. Consider the following two-qubit density operator ρAB of Alice and Bob:

                   ρAB = p1 |Φ+ ⟩⟨Φ+ |AB + p2 |Φ− ⟩⟨Φ− |AB + p3 |Ψ+ ⟩⟨Ψ+ |AB + p4 |Ψ− ⟩⟨Ψ− |AB ,                 (1)

  where p1 , p2 , p3 , p4 are probabilities (p1 , p2 , p3 , p4 ∈ [0, 1] and p1 + p2 + p3 + p4 = 1) and we recall the
  two-qubit Bell state vectors:
                                     1                                1
                            |Φ± ⟩ = √ (|0, 0⟩ ± |1, 1⟩),     |Ψ± ⟩ = √ (|0, 1⟩ ± |1, 0⟩).                        (2)
                                      2                                2
  Suppose that Alice and Bob both measure their qubits with respect to the Pauli-z basis; i.e., the POVM
  is {|0⟩⟨0|, |1⟩⟨1|}. What is the probability that they obtain different measurement outcomes?


6. Consider the state vector |Ψ− ⟩AB of Alice and Bob, defined in (2).
   (a) If Alice and Bob both measure in the computational basis, then how are their outcomes correlated?
   (b) For every measurement outcome of Alice, calculate the corresponding post-measurement state of Bob.
   (c) Let U ∈ L(C2 ) be an arbitrary 2×2 unitary matrix. Prove that (U ⊗U )|Ψ− ⟩⟨Ψ− |(U ⊗U )† = |Ψ− ⟩⟨Ψ− |.
   (d) Conclude that if Alice and Bob both do a measurement with respect to the same but arbitrary
       basis, then their outcomes are always correlated in the same way as in the computational-basis
       measurement.

(c) Consider an arbitrary operator M € L(C?) decomposed in terms of the Pauli operators as M = $(col +
eX + @Y +c¢3Z). Verify that co = Tr[M], cy = Tr[XM], co = Tr[Y M], and cs = Tr[ZM].

Tr[ZM|=p-s.

[89]: | import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

inner_product=0.8

# Parameters

p = (1/2)*(1-inner_product)
n_samples = 20000

# probability of original "1"

# Step 1: sample Bernoulli (0 or 1)
samples = np.random.binomial(1, p, size=n_samples)

# Step 2: map to +1 / -1
mapped = 1-2 * samples #0 ->1, 1 -> -1

# Step 3: running average
running avg = np.cumsum(mapped) / np.arange(1, n_samples + 1)

# True mean of the new variable
true_mean = 1 - 2*p

# Plot

plt.figure()

plt.plot(running avg)#, label="Running average")
plt.axhline(true_mean, linestyle='--', label="True inner product")

plt.xlabel("Number of samples")
plt.ylabel("Sample average")

plt.title("Inner product estimation (swap test)")
plt.legend()

plt.show()

Recap Superdense coding allows Alice to send two bits to Bob using only

The
  qubit        aslong as the qubit is already entangled with Bob's qubit

This worked bc the 4 BellStates were used to encode the information
anddo the measurement          and b c the BellStates are orthogonal they
are perfectly distinguishable



Lethisinteresting

transmit more than one bit of information

So d 2    log 2 1 bit

With entanglement the dimension effectively increases to 4    log141 2

## Poppler embedded text (`pdftotext -layout`)

Problem Bank
                  CS4134 – Quantum Computation and
                        Information Processing
        Sumeet Khatri, Virginia Tech Department of Computer Science, Spring 2026


Table of Contents
Linear algebra                                                                           1

Probability and statistics                                                              8

Quantum mechanics                                                                       11

Entanglement                                                                            16

Quantum circuits                                                                        18

Quantum error correction                                                                22



• Questions marked with a ⋆ are challenging problems that may appear in the exams as bonus
  questions, i.e., they need not be attempted in order to get a full score on the exams.

• You may go the instructor and TA office hours to discuss solutions to the problems.



Linear algebra

1. Consider the complex number z = 1 + 2i.
   (a) Find Re(z).
   (b) Find Im(z).
   (c) Plot z as a point in the complex plane.
   (d) Write z in polar form, z = r eiθ .
   (e) Find z.
   (f) Find |z|.
   (g) Find |z|2 .

2. Prove the following facts:
    (a) For complex numbers z1 , z2 ∈ C, z1 + z2 = z1 + z2
   (b) If |v1 ⟩, |v2 ⟩ ∈ Cd , for any d ∈ {2, 3, . . . }, then ⟨v1 |v2 ⟩ = ⟨v2 |v1 ⟩.

3. Consider the following two-dimensional vector |v⟩ ∈ C2 , written with respect to the standard
   basis {|0⟩, |1⟩}:                                  

    (b) Write the vector |v⟩ in the abstract form |v⟩ = a|0⟩ + b|1⟩, with the appropriate values of a
        and b.
    (c) Is the vector normalized? Say why or why not. If not normalized, then normalize it.

    (c) Is the vector normalized? Say why or why not. If not normalized, then normalize it.

                                                         7
Probability and statistics

1. Fifty teams compete in a student programming competition. It has been observed that 60% of
   the teams use the programming language C while the others use C++, and experience has shown
   that teams who program in C are twice as likely to win as those who use C++. Furthermore, ten
   teams who use C++ include a graduate student, while only four of those who use C include a
   graduate student.
   (a) What is the probability that the winning team programs in C?
   (b) What is the probability that the winning team programs in C and includes a graduate
       student?
   (c) What is the probability that the winning team includes a graduate student?
   (d) Given that the winning team includes a graduate student, what is the probability that team
       programmed in C?

2. Let A be the event that an odd number of spots comes up when a fair die is thrown, and let B
   be the event that the number of spots is a prime number. What is Pr[A|B] and Pr[B|A]?

3. A family has three children. What is the probability that all three children are boys? What is the
   probability that there are two girls and one boy? Given that at least one of the three is a boy, what
   is the probability that all three children are boys. You should assume that Pr[boy] = Pr[girl] = 12 .

4. Three cards are placed in a box; one is white on both sides, one is black on both sides, and the
   third is white on one side and black on the other. One card is chosen at random from the box
   and placed on a table. The (uppermost) face that shows is white. Explain why the probability
   that the hidden face is black is equal to 13 and not 21 .

5. If Pr[A|B] = Pr[B] = Pr[A ∪ B] = 12 , are A and B independent?

6. Let X be a random variable, taking values in {1, 2, 3, . . . }, whose probability mass function is
   given as
                                           αx2 x ∈ {1, 2, 3, 4},
                                         
                                pX (x) =                                                         (33)
                                           0     otherwise.
   (a) What is the value of α?
   (b) Compute Pr[X = 4].
   (c) Compute Pr[X ≤ 2].

7. Let X be a random variable, taking values in {1, 2, 3, . . . }, whose probability masss function is
   given as                              
                                            α/x x ∈ {1, 2, 3, 4}
                                pX (x) =                                                          (34)
                                            0     otherwise
   (a) What is the value of α?
   (b) Compute Pr[X is odd].
   (c) Compute Pr[X > 2].

    (a) Find the marginal probability mass function of X.

11. A coin is tossed 400 times and the number of heads that appear is equal to 225. What is the
    probability that this coin is biased?

                                                  9
12. Messages relayed over a communication channel have probability p of being received correctly. A
    message that is not received correctly is retransmitted until it is. What value should p have so
    that the probability of more than one retransmission is less than 0.05?

13. ⋆ Consider a discrete-time Markov chain consisting of four states, a, b, c, and d, whose transition
    probability matrix is given by                            
                                             0 0 0.8 0.2
                                           0 0.4 0 0.3
                                      P = 1 0.6 0.2 0 
                                                                                                  (45)
                                             0 0       0 0.5
    Compute the following probabilities.
     (a) Pr[X4 = c, X3 = c, X2 = c, X1 = c|X0 = a]
     (b) Pr[X6 = d, X5 = c, X4 = b|X3 = a]
     (c) Pr[X5 = c, X6 = a, X7 = c, X8 = c|X4 = b, X3 = d].

14. ⋆ A Markov chain with two states, a and b, has the following conditional probabilities: if it is in
    state a at time step t, t ∈ {0, 1, 2, . . . }, then it stays in state a with probability 12 ( 12 )t . If it is in
    state b at time step t, then it stays in state b with probability 34 ( 14 )t .
     (a) Determine the transition probability matrix of the Markov chain.

    basis for (C2 )⊗n , and thereby conclude that the set {|GHZz,⃗x ⟩⟨GHZz,⃗x |}z∈{0,1}, ⃗x∈{0,1}n−1 is a

24. ⋆ Fusing two GHZ state vectors. Consider a GHZ state of three qubits and a GHZ state of four
    qubits. We can merge these to create a larger GHZ state of six qubits using the following protocol,
    which is similar to the teleportation protocol.

    Step 1 Apply the CNOT gate to the third qubit of the first GHZ state (which is the control
           qubit) and the first qubit of the second GHZ state (which is the target qubit).
    Step 2 Then, measure the target qubit in the {|0⟩, |1⟩} basis.
    Step 3 If the measurement outcome is “0”, do nothing; if the outcome is “1”, then apply the
           Pauli-X gate to all of the remaining qubits of the second GHZ state.

    Prove that, with probability one, this procedure results in the larger GHZ state of six qubits.

25. ⋆ Let ρ and σ be quantum states. Consider a very simple hypothesis testing strategy for guessing
    whether a given quantum system is in state ρ or σ: Bob discards the state of the system and
    guesses “ρ” with probability q and “σ” with probability 1 − q.
     (a) What is the POVM corresponding to this strategy?
     (b) Evaluate the type-I and type-II error probabilities for this strategy.
     (c) If, in the symmetric setting, the prior probability for being given the state ρ is p ∈ [0, 1],
         then evaluate the expected error probability for this strategy.

26. ⋆ Consider states ρ and σ along with a POVM {M0 , M1 } representing a strategy for hypothesis
    testing of a single copy of the quantum system, where the outcome “0” corresponds to ρ and the
    outcome “1” corresponds to σ. Let p ∈ [0, 1] be the prior probability of being given ρ, and let
                                                (n)    (n)
    n ∈ {2, 3, . . . }. Construct the POVM {Mρ , Mσ } and evaluate the type-I and type-II error
    probabilities for the following two strategies for hypothesis testing of n copies of the quantum
    system.
     (a) The majority-vote strategy: (1) Measure each system according to the POVM {M0 , M1 },
         and let Nx be the number of times the outcome x ∈ {0, 1} occurs; (2) If N0 > N1 , guess
         “ρ”, and if N1 > N0 , guess “σ”. If n is even and N0 = N1 , then guess “ρ” with probability
         q ∈ [0, 1] and “σ” with probability 1 − q.
     (b) The unanimous-vote strategy: (1) Measure each system according to the POVM {M0 , M1 },
         and let Nx be the number of times the outcome x ∈ {0, 1} occurs. (2) If N0 = n, then guess
         “ρ”; otherwise, guess “σ”.

1. A logical qubit is in the state given by the vector |ψ⟩ = 23 |0L ⟩ + 12 |1L ⟩. We encode the logical
   qubit into three physical qubits according to |0L ⟩ = |0, 0, 0⟩ and |1L ⟩ = |1, 1, 1⟩. You suspect that
   a partial bit flip has occurred to one of the qubits, so you measure the parity of adjacent qubits.
    (a) If parity(q1 , q2 ) = 0 and parity(q0 , q1 ) = 0, what quantum gate(s), if any, should you apply
        to fix the error?
    (b) If parity(q1 , q2 ) = 0 and parity(q0 , q1 ) = 1, what quantum gate(s), if any, should you apply
        to fix the error?
    (c) If parity(q1 , q2 ) = 1 and parity(q0 , q1 ) = 0, what quantum gate(s), if any, should you apply
        to fix the error? If parity(q1 , q2 ) = 1 and parity(q0 , q1 ) = 1, what quantum gate(s), if any,
        should you apply to fix the error?

Probability and statistics

Fifty teams compete in a student programming competition. It has been observed that 60% of
the teams use the programming language C while the others use C++, and experience has shown
that teams who program in C are twice as likely to win as those who use C++. Furthermore, ten
teams who use C++ include a graduate student, while only four of those who use C include a
graduate student.

(a) What is the probability that the winning team programs in C?

(b) What is the probability that the winning team programs in C and includes a graduate
student?

(c) What is the probability that the winning team includes a graduate student?

(d) Given that the winning team includes a graduate student, what is the probability that team
programmed in C?

Let A be the event that an odd number of spots comes up when a fair die is thrown, and let B
be the event that the number of spots is a prime number. What is Pr[A|B] and Pr[B|A]?

A family has three children. What is the probability that all three children are boys? What is the
probability that there are two girls and one boy? Given that at least one of the three is a boy, what
is the probability that all three children are boys. You should assume that Pr[boy] = Pr[girl] = 3.

Three cards are placed in a box; one is white on both sides, one is black on both sides, and the
third is white on one side and black on the other. One card is chosen at random from the box
and placed on a table. The (uppermost) face that shows is white. Explain why the probability
that the hidden face is black is equal to 4 and not 3

. If Pr[A|B] = Pr[B] = Pr[AU B] = 3, are A and B independent?

qubits. We can merge these to create a larger GHZ state of six qubits using the following protocol,
which is similar to the teleportation protocol.

Step 1 Apply the CNOT gate to the third qubit of the first GHZ state (which is the control
qubit) and the first qubit of the second GHZ state (which is the target qubit).

Step 2 Then, measure the target qubit in the {|0),|1)} basis.

Step 3 If the measurement outcome is “0”, do nothing; if the outcome is “1”, then apply the
Pauli-X gate to all of the remaining qubits of the second GHZ state.

Prove that, with probability one, this procedure results in the larger GHZ state of six qubits.

* Let p and o be quantum states. Consider a very simple hypothesis testing strategy for guessing
whether a given quantum system is in state p or a: Bob discards the state of the system and
guesses “p” with probability g and “o” with probability 1— q.
(a) What is the POVM corresponding to this strategy?
(b) Evaluate the type-I and type-II error probabilities for this strategy.
(c) If, in the symmetric setting, the prior probability for being given the state p is p € [0,1],
then evaluate the expected error probability for this strategy.

* Consider states p and o along with a POVM {Mo, M1} representing a strategy for hypothesis
testing of a single copy of the quantum system, where the outcome “0” corresponds to p and the
outcome “1” corresponds to a. Let p € [0,1] be the prior probability of being given p, and let
n € {2,3,...}. Construct the POVM (mM, Ms} and evaluate the type-I and type-II error
probabilities for the following two strategies for hypothesis testing of n copies of the quantum
system.

(a) The majority-vote strategy: (1) Measure each system according to the POVM {Mo, Mi},
and let Nz be the number of times the outcome x € {0,1} occurs; (2) If No > Ni, guess
“op”, and if N; > No, guess “o”. If n is even and No = Nj, then guess “p” with probability
q € [0,1] and “o” with probability 1 — q.

(b) The unanimous-vote strategy: (1) Measure each system according to the POVM {Mo, M4},
and let N, be the number of times the outcome x € {0,1} occurs. (2) If No = n, then guess
“op”; otherwise, guess “oa”.

Quantum error correction

1. A logical qubit is in the state given by the vector |) = 3107) + 3|11). We encode the logical
qubit into three physical qubits according to |0;) = |0,0,0) and |1,) = |1,1,1). You suspect that
a partial bit flip has occurred to one of the qubits, so you measure the parity of adjacent qubits.
(a) If parity(q, q2) = 0 and parity(go, qi) = 0, what quantum gate(s), if any, should you apply

to fix the error?
(b) If parity(qi,q2) = 0 and parity(qo,q) = 1, what quantum gate(s), if any, should you apply

to fix the error?
(c) If parity(q1, q2) = 1 and parity(qo,q) = 0, what quantum gate(s), if any, should you apply
to fix the error? If parity(q1, q2) = 1 and parity(qo,q) = 1, what quantum gate(s), if any,

should you apply to fix the error?
